<h4>A-1</h4>
<p><b>abase</b><br/>To lower in position, estimation, or the like; degrade.</p>
<p><b>abbess</b><br/>The lady superior of a nunnery.</p>
<p><b>abbey</b><br/>The group of buildings which collectively form the dwelling-place of a society of monks or nuns.</p>
<p><b>abbot</b><br/>The superior of a community of monks.</p>
<p><b>abdicate</b><br/>To give up (royal power or the like).</p>
<p><b>abdomen</b><br/>In mammals, the visceral cavity between the diaphragm and the pelvic floor; the belly.</p>
<p><b>abdominal</b><br/>Of, pertaining to, or situated on the abdomen.</p>
<p><b>abduction</b><br/>A carrying away of a person against his will, or illegally.</p>
<p><b>abed</b><br/>In bed; on a bed.</p>
<p><b>aberration</b><br/>Deviation from a right, customary, or prescribed course.</p>
<p><b>abet</b><br/>To aid, promote, or encourage the commission of (an offense).</p>
<p><b>abeyance</b><br/>A state of suspension or temporary inaction.</p>
<p><b>abhorrence</b><br/>The act of detesting extremely.</p>
<p><b>abhorrent</b><br/>Very repugnant; hateful.</p>
<p><b>abidance</b><br/>An abiding.</p>
<p><b>abject</b><br/>Sunk to a low condition.</p>
<p><b>abjure</b><br/>To recant, renounce, repudiate under oath.</p>
<p><b>able-bodied</b><br/>Competent for physical service.</p>
<p><b>ablution</b><br/>A washing or cleansing, especially of the body.</p>
<p><b>abnegate</b><br/>To renounce (a right or privilege).</p>
<p><b>abnormal</b><br/>Not conformed to the ordinary rule or standard.</p>
<p><b>abominable</b><br/>Very hateful.</p>
<p><b>abominate</b><br/>To hate violently.</p>
<p><b>abomination</b><br/>A very detestable act or practice.</p>
<p><b>aboriginal</b><br/>Primitive; unsophisticated.</p>
<p><b>aborigines</b><br/>The original of earliest known inhabitants of a country.</p>
<p><b>aboveboard</b><br/>Without concealment, fraud, or trickery.</p>
<p><b>abrade</b><br/>To wear away the surface or some part of by friction.</p>
<p><b>abrasion</b><br/>That which is rubbed off.</p>
<p><b>abridge</b><br/>To make shorter in words, keeping the essential features, leaning out minor particles.</p>
<p><b>abridgment</b><br/>A condensed form as of a book or play.</p>
<p><b>abrogate</b><br/>To abolish, repeal.</p>
<p><b>abrupt</b><br/>Beginning, ending, or changing suddenly or with a break.</p>
<p><b>abscess</b><br/>A Collection of pus in a cavity formed within some tissue of the body.</p>
<p><b>abscission</b><br/>The act of cutting off, as in a surgical operation.</p>
<p><b>abscond</b><br/>To depart suddenly and secretly, as for the purpose of escaping arrest.</p>
<p><b>absence</b><br/>The fact of not being present or available.</p>
<p><b>absent-minded</b><br/>Lacking in attention to immediate surroundings or business.</p>
<p><b>absolution</b><br/>Forgiveness, or passing over of offenses.</p>
<p><b>absolve</b><br/>To free from sin or its penalties.</p>
<p><b>absorb</b><br/>To drink in or suck up, as a sponge absorbs water.</p>
<p><b>absorption</b><br/>The act or process of absorbing.</p>
<p><b>abstain</b><br/>To keep oneself back (from doing or using something).</p>
<p><b>abstemious</b><br/>Characterized by self denial or abstinence, as in the use of drink, food.</p>
<p><b>abstinence</b><br/>Self denial.</p>
<p><b>abstruse</b><br/>Dealing with matters difficult to be understood.</p>
<p><b>absurd</b><br/>Inconsistent with reason or common sense.</p>
<p><b>abundant</b><br/>Plentiful.</p>
<p><b>abusive</b><br/>Employing harsh words or ill treatment.</p>
<p><b>abut</b><br/>To touch at the end or boundary line.</p>
<p><b>abyss</b><br/>Bottomless gulf.</p>
<p><b>academic</b><br/>Of or pertaining to an academy, college, or university.</p>

<p><b>academy</b><br/>Any institution where the higher branches of learning are taught.</p>
<p><b>accede</b><br/>To agree.</p>
<p><b>accelerate</b><br/>To move faster.</p>
<p><b>accept</b><br/>To take when offered.</p>

<p><b>accost</b><br/>To speak to.</p>
<p><b>account</b><br/>A record or statement of receipts and expenditures, or of business transactions.</p>
<p><b>accouter</b><br/>To dress.</p>
<p><b>accredit</b><br/>To give credit or authority to.</p>

<p><b>acerbity</b><br/>Sourness, with bitterness and astringency.</p>

<p><b>ache</b><br/>To be in pain or distress.</p>

<p><b>achromatic</b><br/>Colorless,</p>
<p><b>acid</b><br/>A sour substance.</p>

<p><b>acknowledge</b><br/>To recognize; to admit the genuineness or validity of.</p>
<p><b>acknowledgment</b><br/>Recognition.</p>
<p><b>acme</b><br/>The highest point, or summit.</p>
<p><b>acoustic</b><br/>Pertaining to the act or sense of hearing.</p>
<p><b>acquaint</b><br/>To make familiar or conversant.</p>
<p><b>acquiesce</b><br/>To comply; submit.</p>

<p><b>acquit</b><br/>To free or clear, as from accusation.</p>
<p><b>acquittal</b><br/>A discharge from accusation by judicial action.</p>

<h4>A-4</h4>
<p><b>anthropology</b><br/>The science of man in general.</p>

<p><b>anticlimax</b><br/>A gradual or sudden decrease in the importance or impressiveness of what is said.</p>
<p><b>anticyclone</b><br/>An atmospheric condition of high central pressure, with currents flowing outward.</p>
<p><b>antidote</b><br/>Anything that will counteract or remove the effects of poison, disease, or the like.</p>
<p><b>antilogy</b><br/>Inconsistency or contradiction in terms or ideas.</p>
<p><b>antipathize</b><br/>To show or feel a feeling of antagonism, aversion, or dislike.</p>
<p><b>antiphon</b><br/>A response or alteration of responses, generally musical.</p>
